## [2026-06-25] ingest | PR #41 Phase 2.5 brainstorming xref (merged fd3e5e1). One-bullet additive change to skills/agentic-loop/SKILL.md Phase 2.5: design agent now applies [[brainstorming]]'s design-quality discipline (YAGNI, design-for-isolation, weigh viable approaches) without brainstorming's human-approval gates. Rationale: brainstorming is human-gated by construction; the autonomous loop reuses the design thinking by reference, not by invoking the gated skill. Same reference-not-embody pattern as PR #39. Durable point: "why doesn't the loop just invoke brainstorming?" → brainstorming blocks on a human at its approval gates; Phase 2.5 borrows its *criteria*, not its control flow. Created: sources/pr_41_phase25-brainstorming-xref.md. Updated: skills/agentic-loop.md (Phase 2.5 table row, new § "Phase 2.5 — brainstorming design-quality by reference", Cross-references entry, source in frontmatter); index.md (new source entry).

## [2026-06-25] ingest | PR #42 skills-hooks seam (merged fbe24f1). Four changes: (F4, headline bug) enforce_pr_workflow Gate 3 regex `\bgit +merge\b` also matched `git merge-base` — POSIX ERE `-` is a word boundary, so `\bmerge\b` fires inside `merge-base`. Fixed to `\bgit +merge([[:space:]]|$)` at both Gate 3 and subcommand-detection; new Case 14 test asserts git merge-base → allow. (F2) git-merge block-message hint reordered to lead with resolution (run /pr-review-toolkit:review-pr first), matching the adjacent gh pr merge hint. (F1) finishing-a-development-branch Option 1 gained a note that enforce_pr_workflow blocks git merge on main unless review-pr ran. (F3) New "Skills↔hooks seam convention" in CLAUDE.md: each direction has a cross-reference obligation (skill → name hook + resolution; hook → update instructing skills). wiki-ingest and wiki-lint gained accurate hook-awareness notes; subagent-driven-development deliberately untouched (uses only read-only git merge-base). Created: sources/pr_42_skills-hooks-seam.md; design/skills-hooks-seam.md. Updated: hooks/enforce_pr_workflow.md (merge-base exclusion section, regex before/after, reordered hint, new See Also entry, sources frontmatter); skills/finishing-a-development-branch.md (Hook-gated actions section, sources frontmatter); index.md (new design row + source entry).

## [2026-06-26] ingest | PR #44 no_edit_on_main plugin-source gate + docs/superpowers removal (merged 8179b31). Change 1: no_edit_on_main.sh now gates `skills/*/SKILL.md` and `commands/*.md` on main/master like code files — plugin source carried in markdown is source, not docs (the old docs-only carve-out had let a SKILL.md edit land direct on main earlier the same session). Two `/`-anchored path arms added to the gated `case` (`*/skills/*/SKILL.md|skills/*/SKILL.md`, `*/commands/*.md|commands/*.md`); test suite 11→17 cases. Connected decision: `git push` deliberately NOT gated — edit-time is the correct seam; a push gate would be redundant (edit blocked + branch protection), break the workflow's feature-branch push, and is brittle to match. Also closed finding #4 of a 5-tension agentic-loop review (the #42 seam convention unapplied to the loop's own Phase 3/3a worker prompts, fixed in 4ac38bd); the other 4 tensions were owned tradeoffs, not defects. Change 2: removed historical `docs/superpowers` A–E + self-containment spec/plan tree (~4,500 lines, main-branch hygiene; [[self-containment]] unaffected). Created: sources/pr_44_no-edit-plugin-source.md. Updated: hooks/no_edit_on_main.md (gated-set logic, block condition, plugin-source + git-push-non-gating design notes, sources frontmatter, last_updated); index.md (no_edit_on_main hook row, new source entry, last_updated).

## [2026-06-26] ingest | PR #46 gate git push on main/master (merged 7a4906c). enforce_pr_workflow.sh gains a fourth gated subcommand, `git_push`, mirroring the #40 `git merge` gate: a `git push` landing on main/master is blocked (when workflow.config.yaml exists / opt-in) unless `/pr-review-toolkit:review-pr` ran this session. Key design: Gate 4b for git_push keys off the push DESTINATION, not just the checked-out branch — it gates when (a) current branch is main/master OR (b) the command names an explicit main/master destination refspec (`HEAD:main`, `feature:master`, `:refs/heads/main`). Destination anchor `:(refs/heads/)?(main|master)([[:space:];&|)]|$)` accepts whitespace/EOL/shell-separator so `HEAD:main;echo` can't evade. Documented limitation: bare positional `git push origin main` from off-main is NOT parsed (low risk — pushes local main, which tracks origin/main); feature-branch pushes never gated (PR flow requires them). Process point: pr-review-toolkit multi-agent review caught a Critical silent false-allow in the first impl (current-branch-only let `HEAD:main` refspec pushes through), fixed by destination-refspec gating + a metachar-anchor follow-up, each TDD'd; enforce suite 14→27 cases. NOT a reversal of #44's "don't gate git push" — that was no_edit_on_main edit-seam protection; this is review-evidence enforcement in a different hook. Created: sources/pr_46_gate-git-push-on-main.md. Updated: hooks/enforce_pr_workflow.md (header, logic summary Gate 3/4b, block condition, new "git push gate: destination-refspec model" section, sources frontmatter, last_updated); design/skills-hooks-seam.md (new `git push` row in gated-actions table, sources frontmatter, last_updated); index.md (enforce_pr_workflow hook row, new source entry).

## [2026-06-29] ingest | PR #74 merged (55e0d63): config.test.sh watchdog stalled 5s/call. The #72 watchdog was correct but every resolve() paid the full 5s sleep (~25s of the ~45s suite; low CPU% was the tell). Root cause: `kill $w` orphans the watchdog's `sleep` child, which holds the $() pipe write-fd open, so $() blocks 5s — a pipe-fd lifetime issue, NOT the "ignores SIGTERM" the first comment claimed (empirically false: subshell dies in ~3ms). Fix: `pkill -P $w` kills the sleep directly (closes fd); `{ } 2>/dev/null` swallows the job-control notice. Suite ~45s→~21s, still 15/15, TIMEOUT path intact. Review: comment-analyzer caught the false comment (rewritten in f9a2fbc); code-reviewer self-retracted a wrong narrower-redirect proposal; simplifier ship-as-is; /security-review clean. Pages: sources/pr_74_config-test-watchdog-stall.md (new), sources/pr_72_config-walkup-symlink-hang.md (Follow-up backref), index.md.

## [2026-06-29] ingest | PR #75 merged (feaefe9): main() in scripts/lib/git-common.sh returned blank instead of falling back to literal `main` when `git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD` was unset. Pipeline-exit-status bug: `git ... | sed ... || echo main` — the `||` binds to the pipeline's exit (sed's, 0 on empty input), so the fallback never fired. Fix: capture + `echo "${m:-main}"` (key off empty output). Latent — origin/HEAD is set by clone/gh, so only bare-`git init` test scaffolding hit the blank; starved sync::main_branch (added by un-ingested #73) into a silent no-op. Regression test added (marker-less repo → must yield `main`). 3 reviews (code/tests/silent-failure) clean, 0 findings. Same pipeline-mechanism family as #74. Pages: sources/pr_75_main-branch-fallback.md (new), index.md. Note: #73 (sync::main_branch origin) has no source page — never ingested.

## [2026-06-29] ingest | PR #76 merged (37459a3): harden hook stdin read — replaced `input=$(cat)` with `IFS= read -r -d '' -t 5 input || true` in all 10 hook scripts. ## [2026-06-30] ingest | PR #80 merged (f5aacde): guard both halves of the timeout invariant — extends `hooks_json_timeout_floor.test.sh` with Half B. Closes test-analyzer S1 from PR #78's review. Half A (PR #78): `min(hooks.json declared timeout) >= 5`. Half B (this PR): exactly 10 hook scripts carry the bounded-read backstop, and every `read -t N` == 5. Together both halves make the full `read -t 5 <= min(hooks.json timeout)` invariant tamper-evident: a future PR that lowers the in-process `read -t` value alone OR a hook silently gaining/losing the backstop now fails the suite. ## [2026-07-05] ingest | PRs #96–98 merged (cluster, 127a149/76084fe/559d79b): mode-aware install sweep, command-substitution injection class closed, hook-owned loop-stop counter. #96: `install.sh`'s exec-bit sweep reads each swept file's git index mode and branches (100755→ensure +x, 100644→ensure -x [new], not-in-index→legacy unconditional +x), closing the index-vs-installed-copy drift PR #94 flagged. New test `install_mode_sweep.test.sh` uses a real git worktree so `git ls-files -s` matches the real index. Fix round closed a Critical: the mode-read line ran under `set -euo pipefail`, and `git ls-files` exits 128 outside a git repo (release-tarball installs), silently killing the installer after the first swept file — fixed with `|| _index_mode=""` falling through to the pre-existing fallback branch; RED-first regression test added (no-`.git` directory, asserts exit 0 + fallback still applies). Suite 24→25. #97: experimentally proved [[post-review]]'s PR #93 render-time PR-state line was a **command-substitution injection**, not the milder "unsanitised input" PR #93 itself had noted — `$ARGUMENTS` is textually spliced into a render-time `` !`cmd` `` line before the shell parses it, so a payload executes as live shell syntax regardless of surrounding quotes (quoting only governs interpretation after substitution, not the substitution itself). Two reviewers had rated the original note low-severity without testing command substitution; this experimental methodology (running a real payload) caught what static review twice missed. Fix: removed the injected block entirely, replaced with argument-free `gh pr list --state open --limit 10` (matches merge.md's convention); `## Step 0 — Argument gate` rewritten as pure model-level inspection (never paste the argument into a shell command); added a **class-wide test** banning `$ARGUMENTS` in any `commands/*.md` render-time `` !`cmd` `` line. RED: 2 genuine fails + 1 unrelated BSD-grep bug in the test itself, also fixed. GREEN: 10/10. Suite 24/24 (net unchanged — 2 lines removed, replaced by different-shaped guard). #98: `loop_stall_guard.sh` becomes the sole writer of `progress.json.loop_stop_counts`, closing a two-writer lost-update race (hook's presence check + orchestrator self-maintenance prose in SKILL.md) that had undercounted 2 loops in a recorded session. New `bump_loop_stop_count()` does a tmp-file jq read-modify-write (auto-vivifying), same pattern as `post_review.sh`'s `write_cache`; best-effort and never fatal (missing file/malformed JSON/failed mv all logged and swallowed, hook still exits 0). `SKILL.md` updated in 5 places (body only) to mark the field HOOK-OWNED, mirroring `completed_marker`'s existing carry-forward treatment. Fix round added 4 standing-invariant tests: no-clobber (other progress.json keys survive byte-identical), jq-absence fail-open (`command -v jq || return 0`), last-declaration-wins tie-break for multi-`LOOP-STOP` messages, degraded-filesystem safety (unwritable/never-created directories) — plus found and fixed an off-by-one in the test harness's own `run_env` helper (arg0-pinning shifted args, producing a false exit-127 on the jq-absence test). `loop_stall_guard.test.sh` 13→21. Suite 24/24 both rounds. Context: repo renamed to `blueman82/coderails-dev` mid-loop (old URLs redirect); local `~/.claude` ai_docs hooks/subagents/slash-commands snapshots refreshed (hooks 8→29 events) after the stale-snapshot pattern from PR #89–91 recurred; an org-auth outage killed a worker mid-fix-round (uncommitted worktree work survived, versioned respawn inherited it); origin/main advanced under the loop twice (workers switched to merge-base-relative scope assertions). ## [2026-07-06] ingest | PRs #11–14 merged: gate-hardening follow-ups (tier-0 NO-GO precedence, HOME-sandboxed install test, push.sh staging fix, trust-floor widened + merge.sh error split)
Four independent work-units, base 238f5e1 (post-PR#10), each requiring both a review artifact and an eval artifact before merge. #11 (`a1c4803`, owner directive): `hooks/scripts/lib/loop_state_common.sh`'s `als_read_loop_evals_result()` now checks explicit `result == "NO-GO"` before the tier-0 exemption branch — previously a tier-0 artifact with an explicit recorded `NO-GO` still read as the allowed `TIER0` case, since the exemption fired on tier alone. "An exemption justifies having no evals, not overriding a recorded failure." A tier-0 artifact with no `result` set at all (the legitimate exemption) is unaffected. #12 (`fdd29fd`): `install_mode_sweep.test.sh` now sandboxes `$HOME` for both `install.sh` invocations it makes — closes a **real, recurring corruption** of the developer machine's actual `~/.claude/settings.json` (10 auto-repaired events during this very loop, caused by `test_gate`'s per-commit test run executing inside worker worktrees carrying the unfixed test; `MEMORY_TARGET` alone never redirected install.sh's unconditional `$HOME` writes). Anti-vacuity discipline: pre-seeds a stale marketplace key so the sandbox mutation is proven real, not merely inert; before/after cksum guards on the real settings.json/known_marketplaces.json/CLAUDE.md. #13 (`321bca3`): `push.sh` staging changed `git add -A` → `git add -u` + a named untracked-file warning (explicit `git add` now needed for new-file PRs); review caught and fixed a `grep '^??'`-under-`pipefail` crash on the zero-untracked-files case (`865cab0`); new `hooks/scripts/tests/push_staging.test.sh` (first-ever dedicated staging coverage); `docs/REFERENCE.md` updated. #14 (`7c1dd19`, security-relevant, owner directive): the review/eval artifact gates' `author_association == "OWNER"` trust conjunct — which failed closed on org-owned repos ([[pr_7-10_task-evals-followups|PR #8]]'s own documented scoped limitation) — is **removed entirely** (clean break, independently verified no surviving compat path) and replaced with a repo-permission check: login match (unchanged anti-spoof) **AND** `viewerPermission` of `ADMIN`/`MAINTAIN`/`WRITE` on the current repo (new `pr::_trusted_permission`/`pr::_permission_is_write_or_better` in `scripts/lib/git-common.sh`); a resolvable-but-insufficient permission is "no trusted comment found," not a fetch failure; an actual lookup failure still fails closed. `merge.sh`'s two artifact gates also gained a three-way error-message split (identity/permission/comments-fetch failure) via a new `PR_TRUST_FETCH_FAIL_REASON` signal threaded through a `pr::_trusted_comment_bodies_or_fail` wrapper (stderr-carried, since the reader is always called via `$(...)`). `INSTALLATION.md` documents the new trust rule for operators. New 6-check TDD smoke test — first test infrastructure for any SDD script. Clean-break: no shim, no fallback to the old path; accepted one-time migration risk for any in-flight ledger at merge time (recovery: `git log` remains authoritative, per the skill's pre-existing contract). #17 (F1, `d1b1360`): new sibling Stop hook `hooks/scripts/unregistered_loop_guard.sh` — nudges (`additionalContext`, exit 0), never blocks, when ≥3 DISTINCT `message.id` values carry an `Agent` tool_use (parallel fan-outs share one message.id and never trip it; sequential dispatches — the incident's actual shape — each get a distinct id) AND no `progress.json` at the resolved path AND no `agentic-loop` Skill invocation anywhere in the transcript. Deliberate deviation from every sibling loop-state hook (all of which block on ground truth): this hook has only a heuristic, so nudge is the honest posture; the flip-to-block condition is pre-recorded (a nudge delivered but ignored escalates it). `jq` failures logged with distinct reasons (`jq_missing`/`jq_parse_error`/`payload_parse_error`), never folded into the below-threshold case. STALE PAGES: unchanged, same 7 point-in-time records plus `design/hook-exit-codes.md` (flagged prior pass, still accurate, not re-flagged as a new finding). MISSING CONCEPTS: 0 new. MISSING CROSS-REFS: 0 new. DATA GAPS: 0 — this cluster is test-file + single-script content, no new command/hook/skill surface introduced. INBOX: 0 backlog (directory does not exist).

## [2026-07-06] ingest | PRs #23–24 merged: Loop 2's second follow-ups cluster (hook-lib failure observability + repo-keyed loop state)
Two PRs treated as one cluster (wu1 + wu2 of a 3-unit follow-ups loop; wu3's three editorial pages were delivered in a separate pass, already logged above). #23 (`9837c15`): `als_count_invocations` (`hooks/scripts/lib/loop_state_common.sh`) no longer logs a jq-failure reason directly via `als_log` on every call — under `als_stable_invocations`'s retry loop this made a transient failure that recovered on a later attempt indistinguishable from one that never recovered, and a sustained failure logged once per attempt with no final verdict (reproduced empirically: a persistently-malformed transcript produced 2 identical lines at `MAX_ATTEMPTS=3`). Fix: the function now signals `jq_missing`/`jq_parse_error` on **stderr** instead (a global can't cross the retry caller's command-substitution subshell boundary); `als_stable_invocations` captures stderr per attempt via a scratch file (`mktemp`, fails open per the PR #21 tempfile lesson) and logs exactly one summary line after the retry loop exits (`reason=X attempts=N outcome=recovered|exhausted`), never per-attempt. One-shot caller `unregistered_loop_guard.sh`'s `ulg_has_skill_invocation` now explicitly discards the new stderr signal (`2>/dev/null`), preserving its prior silent-on-parse-failure behaviour as an explicit choice. Also fixed a real, separate `als_log` bug: a trailing `2>/dev/null` on `printf` alone does not suppress a redirection-open error (e.g. missing `LOG_FILE` parent) — fixed via a brace-group wrapping the whole statement; accepted tradeoff documented (a missing LOG_FILE parent still silently swallows a caller's own failure-reporting line too, only reachable via a misconfigured `CLAUDE_DISCIPLINE_LOG` override). Verified: gate outcomes proven bit-identical to the pre-change build via a cross-SHA consumer exit-code matrix (3 consumers × 4 fixtures). #24 (`14c7f1c`): `agentic_loop_path.sh`'s slug is now derived from `git -C "$cwd" rev-parse --path-format=absolute --git-common-dir` when cwd is in a git repo, instead of the raw cwd — all worktrees of one repo now share one `progress.json`, closing a real, live-observed bug where a mid-loop `EnterWorktree` hop (now a prescribed part of the shared-checkout workflow per the 2026-07-06 user directive) silently orphaned a loop's state onto a new cwd-keyed path. Critical fix caught by review: a git older than 2.31 doesn't recognise `--path-format`, echoes it back verbatim alongside a RELATIVE path, and exits 0 — trusting any non-empty stdout would have collapsed every old-git-host repo onto one garbage shared slug; fixed by validating the captured value is actually an absolute path before use, falling through to the cwd-slug fallback otherwise (same as an outright git failure). Sanitisation collisions (`"foo/bar"`==`"foo_bar"`) documented as an accepted tradeoff (replacement over fresh-fallback, since session_id is harness-owned not attacker-controlled) at both duplicate transform sites, kept intentionally un-shared (`agentic_loop_path.sh` stays dependency-free), with a pinning test locking the collision itself. Clean-break, no compat flag — old cwd-keyed state dirs left untouched on disk; dashboard's slug-globbing collector verified to still pick up both shapes. **Supersedes [[pr_86_agentic-loop-hardening|PR #86]] point 6's 2026-07-01 rejection** of locking machinery for the single-loop-per-directory race — the workflow shift (prescribed mid-session `EnterWorktree`) changed the calculus; this is a ~15ms keying fix, not the rejected machinery, so the two decisions aren't in tension. **Live proof**: the fix re-keyed this very loop's own `progress.json` mid-flight, from the worktree-cwd slug to the repo-keyed slug, the moment it merged. Created: `sources/pr_23-24_hook-lib-observability-and-repo-keyed-loop-state.md`, `design/agentic-loop-path-keying.md` (new page). Updated: `hooks/loop_state_guard.md` (path-authority section rewritten for the repo-keyed scheme, frontmatter, see-also), `hooks/unregistered_loop_guard.md` (new Known-limitations bullet for the stderr-discard carve-out, frontmatter, see-also), `sources/pr_86_agentic-loop-hardening.md` (superseded-by note appended to point 6, historical text preserved, `last_updated` bumped), `index.md` (new Design-list row, new Sources row).

## [2026-07-06] ingest | PR #25 merged: observability dashboard (sub-project 1 of 5, agentic-OS evolution)
New `coderails:dashboard` skill: a Next.js/React Three Fiber web HUD plus a native Obsidian command-centre plugin, both reading state the kernel already produces (session dirs, agentic-loop `progress.json` via the existing `agentic_loop_path.sh` SSOT, `gh`-polled PR artifact markers parsed with the same marker grammar as `review-artifact.sh`/`eval-artifact.sh`, hook logs, wiki/memory mtimes) — no new services, no telemetry leaving the machine. Seven panels (SYSTEM VITALS, DIRECTIVES, DOCUMENTS/MEMORY.TRAIL, COMMAND DECK, PR GATES, bottom-centre hero, reserved assistant-agent slot). One `POST /api/run` endpoint, token- and Origin-guarded, spawns headless `claude -p` runs through a single profile→flag mapping (`buildArgv` in `src/lib/argv.ts`: read-only/standard/bypass) — the Obsidian plugin reuses it rather than re-implementing. Flag-smuggling closed by two independent layers found during review: a leading-dash `input` value is rejected outright (a `claude -p "--version"` empirical test confirmed the CLI really does parse a leading-dash argument as a flag, not literal text) AND a literal `--` end-of-options sentinel is always inserted before `input` regardless — neither layer alone was judged sufficient. The Obsidian plugin's `agentic-os` code-block processor writes intent files to `~/.claude/coderails-dashboard/queue/`, a deliberately frozen seam for the not-yet-built routines sub-project (2 of 5), with an interim direct-exec path meanwhile; ships a committed reproducible `dist/main.js` build. Process record: 16 SDD tasks each independently reviewed; 5 fix loops (lock TOCTOU Critical, marker grammar drift, `hooksFired` today-scoping, single-SSE-provider requirement, flag-smuggling scanner High). The frozen Tier-2 eval suite (10 evals, required since the PR is both ≥3 work-units and touches an outward/irreversible surface) caught **two production bugs every review round missed**: the launch script reported false-success against a squatted port, and a statically-prerendered page baked an empty button config into the HTML (fixed by forcing the route dynamic) — the first concrete demonstration in this wiki of the task-evals gate catching a real bug in production rather than only exercising its own mechanics. Eval artifact GO 10/10 and review artifact both posted SHA-bound on the PR; `/coderails:merge`'s two gates each consumed their respective artifact. The loop this PR ran under also registered its own loop-scope `evals.json` (GO 4/4, Phase 2.7c). Created: `skills/dashboard.md` (new skill page), `sources/pr_25_observability-dashboard.md`. ## [2026-07-07] ingest | Addendum: loop-state re-keying gap from the same 1.0.0→1.1.0 plugin update
Orchestrator-verified finding, folded into the ASSISTANT.LINK cluster's existing pages rather than a new page (small, single-mechanism addition). The 1.0.0 cache predates [[agentic-loop-path-keying|PR #24]] entirely (verified: no `agentic_loop_path.sh` file exists in that cache directory at all — the older cwd-only slug scheme was all that version had), so the same overnight auto-update that closed the stale-hooks gap ([[assistant-link-send-gate-architecture]]) also silently switched any pre-existing session's `progress.json` path from the legacy cwd-slug to the git-common-dir-keyed slug PR #24 introduced. Unlike the same-version mid-loop re-key case [[agentic-loop-path-keying]] already documented, a plugin-version upgrade gives the active session no advance signal — a maintained loop was reported unregistered by the newer guards post-update. Workaround applied live: a symlink from the new slug to the old state directory. Added as a new caveat to `design/agentic-loop-path-keying.md` (candidate fixes: legacy-slug fallback, or a plugin-update migration step — filed for the owner, not actioned), with matching cross-references added to `design/assistant-link-send-gate-architecture.md` and `design/install-and-cache-trap.md`. This is a migration gap, not a bug fix — nothing in this pass changes `agentic_loop_path.sh`'s behaviour.

## [2026-07-07] ingest | approvals-dir move (coderails PR #62 + assistant-agent PR #10)

The move: the send-gate's own approval files (`gate/surfaces/queue.ts`'s `DEFAULT_QUEUE_DIR`, and the dashboard's matching `api/events`/`api/queue` route constants) moved from `~/.claude/coderails-dashboard/queue/` to a new sibling `approvals/` directory. Root cause captured for the first time in the wiki: `queue/` had grown two other consumers — the routines runner sweep and workflow-audit's `propose-skill` proposal writer ([[pr_43-44-46_workflow-audit-queue-seam]]) — both of which glob every `.json` file in the directory and quarantine/reject anything that isn't their own expected shape; a `QueueFileEntry` approval file looked like malformed input to both, so the send-gate's approval traffic needed its own directory. Clean-break, no dual-dir fallback, nothing to migrate (no prior producer ever wrote approval-shaped files into `queue/`). Created `sources/pr_62_10_approvals-dir-move.md`. Ingested a two-PR cluster (both merged 2026-07-07): PR #70 fixes a real, long-standing bug in the dashboard's button-input delivery (`buildArgv()` split `command` and `input` into two argv positionals, but the `claude` CLI only consumes one, so **every `inputAllowed` button silently dropped user input since the button model's inception** — caught by an intake smoke test, not by any prior argv-shape review round or unit test) plus a new "ask" button pattern it enabled. ## [2026-07-07] query-file-back | run/events/run-log architecture and streaming output-viewer gap

Query: what does the wiki cover about the dashboard's `/api/run` route, `/api/events` SSE stream, and the `runs.jsonl`/`runs/<runId>.log` artifact model, and what would a plan to add a streaming output-viewer need to know that isn't documented. Wiki coverage was architectural-only (`skills/dashboard.md` + its 5 source pages) — no page documented the run-log artifact model as its own topic, and none addressed a streaming viewer (no prior plan, no rejection). Read current source directly (`route.ts`, `events/route.ts`, `runlog.ts`, `collect/index.ts`, `useRunLifecycle.ts`, the design spec) rather than trusting wiki summaries, since this was a "what would a plan need to know" question requiring ground truth. Verified finding: the per-run `.log` file is write-only in the entire codebase — `route.ts` appends `stdout+stderr` to it exactly once, post-exit, inside the `execFile` callback; `RunRecord.outputPath` is stored in `runs.jsonl` but never read anywhere (grep confirms exactly 2 non-test hits: the write site and the type definition); the frontend's only `RunRecord` consumer (`useRunLifecycle.ts`) uses it purely for sphere hue/progress, never renders output text. Also verified the aggregator's recursive `fs.watch` on `runsDir` does fire on `.log` writes but only triggers a `runs.jsonl` metadata re-read — no log bytes ever reach the `Snapshot` or an SSE frame. Filed [[dashboard-run-log-streaming-viewer-gap_2026-07-07]] documenting this plus 6 cross-PR constraints a streaming-viewer plan must respect (Origin/Host guard, strict-ID-validation precedent from the [[pr_31_assistant-link-approve-button]] path-traversal fix, the single-SSE-provider requirement from PR #25's fix-loop, collector never-throw discipline, token/CSRF non-leakage, and the long-lived-POST/lock-lifetime coupling) and 5 assumptions a plan should not make. Updated `index.md`'s Investigations section.

## [2026-07-08] ingest | PRs #80–82 — dashboard streaming output-viewer (closes the 2026-07-07 gap)

Ingested a three-PR cluster (all merged 2026-07-08) as ONE source page, per the cluster's own theme: a real streaming output-viewer for the dashboard, closing [[dashboard-run-log-streaming-viewer-gap_2026-07-07]] the day after that investigation was filed. PR #80 (backend, `2a49d05`): `POST /api/run` now spawns `claude` with `--output-format stream-json --include-partial-messages --verbose`, streams stdout/stderr chunks incrementally to `runs/<runId>.log` (clean break from the old single post-exit write the investigation documented) and publishes each chunk on a new in-process pub/sub `runOutputBus.ts`, re-emitted by the aggregator as a new `"run-output"` SSE event on the existing `/api/events` connection — explicitly not a second SSE endpoint, honouring the investigation's single-SSE-provider constraint. New non-throwing, forward-compatible `streamJson.ts` parser (no event-type allowlist; parse failures never affect what's appended/published). Review caught and fixed a Critical: no `child.on("error", ...)` handler, so a spawn failure would hang the request forever and leak the per-button lock. PR #81 (frontend, `f2371ea`): new `OutputViewerPanel.tsx` in the COMMAND DECK — live-streams an active run from the SSE-accumulated buffer, fetches a finished run's settled output once via new `GET /api/run/output`, which validates `runId` against `/^[0-9a-f]{16}$/` and — going further than the PR #31 path-traversal precedent the investigation cited — never joins `runId` into a path at all, instead reading the matching `RunRecord`'s own server-written `outputPath`. Review caught and fixed a Critical: `fetchSettledOutput` silently swallowed all fetch/parse errors; fixed with a discriminated result type, a distinct 409/in-progress case, a visible retry button, and pruning of the `runOutput` accumulator for runs aged out of run-history. PR #82 (docs, `a383f36`): `docs/REFERENCE.md` + `skills/dashboard/SKILL.md` updated to describe the viewer. Verified all claims directly against `git show origin/main:<path>` for `runOutputBus.ts`, `streamJson.ts`, `api/run/route.ts`, `api/run/output/route.ts`, `OutputViewerPanel.tsx`, `useDashboardState.ts`, `collect/index.ts`, `docs/REFERENCE.md`, and `SKILL.md` — not summarised from a brief alone. Created `sources/pr_80-82_dashboard-stream-run-output-viewer.md`. Updated: `skills/dashboard.md` (new "Run Output viewer" subsection under Architecture, frontmatter sources/tags, See-also), `wiki/investigations/dashboard-run-log-streaming-viewer-gap_2026-07-07.md` (CLOSED banner + `status: closed` frontmatter + point-by-point Resolution section mapping each of the investigation's 7 findings/constraints to how this cluster satisfied it; investigative content left unchanged as a historical record), `index.md` (investigation bullet marked CLOSED, new Sources entry, frontmatter `last_updated`).

## [2026-07-08] ingest | PR #88 + #93 — dashboard launchd agent (reboot survival)

Ingested a two-PR cluster (both merged 2026-07-08) as one source page, theme "dashboard reboot survival via launchd." PR #88 (`ec46132`) gives the dashboard a launchd LaunchAgent — new `launchd/com.coderails.dashboard.plist` (`RunAtLoad`+`KeepAlive`+`ThrottleInterval 60`), a thin exec wrapper `skills/dashboard/runner/bin/dashboard-server.sh` (execs `npm run start` in the foreground; deliberately duplicates ~13 lines of `start-dashboard.sh`'s build-if-stale logic rather than sharing it, extended with a fail-safe dependency/config staleness check and a missing-src-dir rebuild trigger a daemon needs and an interactive script doesn't), `launchd/install-dashboard-agent.sh`/`uninstall-dashboard-agent.sh`, and a mutation-validated static guard suite `hooks/scripts/tests/dashboard_agent.test.sh`. The installer reuses, rather than rediscovers, the boot-persistence fix [[routines]] already documents for the routine-sweeper agents: copy the plist into `~/Library/LaunchAgents/` and bootstrap from that copy, not the repo path — a repo-path bootstrap silently unloads on the next reboot (the routine-sweeper agents hit this live on 2026-07-08: 03:00 run fine, reboot at 07:34, every `com.coderails` job gone). PR #93 (`f630a98`) fixes an uninstall-time race found the same day: `launchctl bootout` is asynchronous for a running `KeepAlive` job (~2s observed to actually unload) — the uninstaller now polls up to 10×1s before declaring failure instead of checking once immediately, and only removes the `~/Library/LaunchAgents/` copy after the loaded-check passes (previously at risk of removing the copy on a still-loading false positive). Verified both PRs directly against `gh pr view --json title,body,files,mergedAt,mergeCommit` and `gh pr diff` rather than relying solely on the team-lead's brief. Design-fork record (thin-exec-wrapper vs. plist-invokes-start-dashboard.sh vs. a `--foreground` flag) captured in the new source page per the brief's own resolved-forks summary. Created `sources/pr_88_93_dashboard-launchd.md`. Updated: `skills/dashboard.md` (new "Surviving reboots (launchd)" subsection under Starting/stopping, frontmatter `sources`/`tags` extended), `design/routines.md` (cross-reference paragraph noting the dashboard reused this page's boot-persistence fix rather than rediscovering it, frontmatter `sources` extended, `last_updated` bumped to 2026-07-08), `index.md` (new Sources entry, chronologically last).

Second commit hardens the check: session_id is escaped (`sed 's/[.[\*^$\\]/\\&/g'`) before interpolation into the grep BRE pattern, closing a wildcard-match false-suppression regression (a literal `.` in a session id could otherwise match an unrelated session's logged line). ## [2026-07-08] ingest | loop-lib residuals cluster (PRs #91/#107/#86/#87/#94) + comment_citation_gate coverage-gap fix

Ingested a five-PR cluster (all merged 2026-07-08) as one source page,
`sources/pr_86-107_2026-07-08_loop-lib-residuals.md`. Main thread: PR #91
(`f1db15c4`) makes the shared `hooks/scripts/lib/loop_state_common.sh`
transcript parse malformed-line-tolerant (per-line `jq -R 'fromjson? //
empty'` pre-filter ahead of the aggregating `jq -s`, dropped lines reported
as `skipped_malformed=N` on stderr) — a single bad JSONL line previously
collapsed the whole invocation count to empty/0, making
`als_gate_require_active_loop` treat a genuinely active loop as "not a loop"
and defeating [[loop_state_guard]], [[loop_stall_guard]], [[voice_announce]],
and (via its delegate call) [[unregistered_loop_guard]]. PR #107 (`d4256542`,
same day, a post-merge 4-reviewer verification pass) corrected two
failure-attribution regressions the tolerant parse had introduced: a
`read_error` tag for an unreadable transcript or a stage-1 `jq` binary death
(previously indistinguishable from "clean"), and an `all_lines_malformed` tag
distinguishing total parse loss (every line malformed) from a benign partial
skip — the distinction gates the `als_stable_invocations` retry/settle loop,
restoring the 5-attempt flush-race window a mis-attributed "clean" result
would have short-circuited. `unregistered_loop_guard.sh`'s own separate
`jq -s` slurp (`ulg_count_dispatch_turns`) and `discipline_common.sh`'s
`dc_extract_last_text` (a different lib family) both carry the identical bare
`jq -s` fragility and were explicitly NOT touched — both recorded as standing
residuals on the source page and cross-linked from
[[unregistered_loop_guard]]'s own page. Smaller, unrelated fixes swept into
the same cluster: PR #86 (`9b300355`) gives the Obsidian command-centre
plugin's `pressButton` (`exec.ts`) a try/catch around `buildArgv`, matching
`route.ts`'s existing parity; PR #87 (`81a705f6`) investigated a reported
nested-worktree test-failure concern in `install_mode_sweep.test.sh` and did
NOT reproduce it (documented as a header comment, no code change); PR #94
(`f4e05ee9`) removes a third-occurrence leaked root `evals.json` and adds a
root-anchored `/evals.json` gitignore entry that doesn't shadow the tracked
dashboard test fixture. **PR-number collision, deliberately avoided:** this
cluster's #86/#87 are unrelated to the older, pre-recreation
`sources/pr_86_agentic-loop-hardening.md` /
`sources/pr_87_agentic-loop-path-session-keying.md` (both merged 2026-07-01)
— left byte-untouched; the new page's slug carries the cluster theme, not a
bare `pr_86_`/`pr_87_` name.

Updated: `hooks/loop_state_guard.md` (new "Malformed-transcript tolerance"
section, frontmatter sources/tags, see-also, `last_updated` 2026-07-06→
2026-07-08), `hooks/loop_stall_guard.md` (cross-reference note in its
skip-gates list, frontmatter sources/tags, see-also, `last_updated`

Design principle recorded on the source page: "visibly-wrong beats plausibly-fabricated" — a `{}` (miner failed open), absent, incomplete, or wrong-typed `.cost` on a `schema_version >= 2` retro each print a DISTINCT honest message, never a fabricated figure; only a legacy `schema_version < 2` retro stays silent. Failed CLOSED (wrongful block, not a bypass) — forced security-review pass (mandatory, diff touches `hooks/`) returned APPROVE. **Not a duplicate of the existing `als_count_invocations` fix already on the vault** (PR #198, same file, same one-line `select(type == "object")` shape, but a DIFFERENT function with the OPPOSITE failure direction: a poisoned line there collapsed the invocation count to 0, causing the entire complete-gate family — retro/work-units/proof — to be skipped as fail-open, the security-classed bug PR #198 fixed; PR #208's bug is fail-closed and correctness-classed). ## [2026-07-17] ingest | PR #207 (merged `70d0fe0`) + PR #209 (merged `dc4f3bb`) ingested as ONE thematic source page, [[pr_207_209_docs-sync-nightly-and-drift-fix]] — a docs-drift fix and the self-merging nightly routine built to replace the mechanism that was supposed to catch that drift automatically but had been broken for 9 days. #207: README skill count 34→35, five missing skill rows added (`dashboard`, `fable-mode`, `sync-docs`, `verify-merged-pr`, `workflow-audit`), `offload_push_guard.sh` hook row added, a new "Sandboxed workers" section documenting PR #199's `scripts/sandbox/*` (no wiki page yet — flagged, not built, out of this cluster's scope), legacy "two separate plugins" origin story and a stale "(claude-guardrails)" title parenthetical removed. #209: ships a **new, separate** skill `docs-sync` (`skills/docs-sync/SKILL.md`) — distinct from the pre-existing `sync-docs` skill it invokes for its audit step — as the `sync-docs-nightly` routine (button `sync-docs`, renamed mid-PR from `docs-sync`, `f3ef802`): audits git-tracked docs nightly and, only if drift is found, edits/pushes/reviews/self-merges a fix with no human in the loop; a no-drift night logs `no-drift` and stops before touching git state. **Root cause, WITH a retraction:** `sync-docs-weekly`'s `foreignSkillPath` pointed at a path that never existed; it ran green 2026-07-08 then correctly escalated red on 2026-07-15 (`dashboard-runs/sync-docs-weekly.md`, verified read in full) — an earlier claim during this investigation that it "failed silently" was FALSE and is retracted on the source page: that claim came from grepping `sweeper.log` (the wrong surface), when `escalate.ts:55-68` (verified, read directly) shows the vault-note escalation fired exactly as designed. The real gap: escalation reached a channel nobody was watching, operationally equivalent to silence for an unattended routine even though mechanically distinct. **Config validation gap** (verified, `config.ts:102-111` + `sweep.ts:243` read directly): `foreignSkillPath` is checked non-empty+absolute, never existence-on-disk — the structural fix taken is needing no `foreignSkillPath` at all (in-repo skill, same as [[loop-retro-promotion]]); zero of five shipped routines use the field now. **`maxAgeSeconds` trap:** it's a manual field, not derived from `cadence` (verified, `config.ts:76-79`) — flipping cadence without re-deriving the freshness bar would silently reintroduce a staleness bug; shipped value correctly narrowed to 129600s (36h) for the nightly cadence. **SECURITY (the most important finding):** the manifest's "diff contains only `.md` files" check is not a path allow-list — the routine's own governing files (`skills/docs-sync/SKILL.md` itself, `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `docs/routines.md`) are all `.md`, so a bare extension check would let it legally rewrite its own safety contract. Two further holes proven **empirically, re-derived live in this ingest session** (commands and output recorded on both the source page and [[routines]]): `git mv scripts/gate.sh evil.md` then `git diff --name-only` prints bare `evil.md` (passes as `.md`, smuggling a renamed script) while `--name-status` exposes `R100 scripts/gate.sh evil.md`; `git rm README.md` under `--name-only` is indistinguishable from an edit, while `--name-status` prints `D README.md`. Fix: `--name-status` (never `--name-only`) + explicit self-governance deny-list + reject R/C whose source wasn't in-scope + reject D of in-scope docs; any violation is ABORT WITH CLEANUP. **Tautological contract tests:** the shipped test file itself documents that `grep -qi 'no-drift'` passes on prose meaning the opposite ("no-drift handling was removed..."), and a reviewer caught an earlier revision that had already silently dropped its whole failure-visibility section while all 14 checks stayed green; fixed by anchoring on normative sentences plus `neg_check` negative controls. **Honest limits, stated plainly:** manifest + deny-list are prompt-enforced only (`PreToolUse` does not fire under `claude -p`, verified in-repo); no branch protection by design; the routine authors its own review/eval artifacts and merges on them — self-attestation is real and unresolved, `.md`-only blast radius is the actual mitigation. Scope was deliberately narrowed vs. the literal "no human involved" ask: it refuses to auto-fix its own governing docs and escalates those to a human. `loop-retro-promotion-weekly`, the precedent this pattern copies, has never fired its full self-merge chain (`promotion-runs.log` shows one `predicate=unmet` line) — making `sync-docs-nightly` this repo's first actual production exercise of the complete headless chain. **Proven live 2026-07-17:** seeder queued it (`1 seeded, 4 not due`), sweeper claimed and ran it (`1 claimed, 1 succeeded, 0 failed`), frozen loop evals E6/E7 passed against the live config — but no drift existed that run, so only the no-drift short-circuit was exercised; the actual self-merge chain (steps 3-9) remains unexercised in production. Updated [[routines]] (new `sync-docs-nightly` section folding in all findings above, retired `sync-docs-weekly` from the shipped-routines list, `foreignSkillPath`/`maxAgeSeconds` guidance updated), created [[docs-sync]] (new skill page), corrected [[sync-docs]] (its "user-level only, not part of coderails" claim was itself stale — the skill moved in-repo 2026-07-10, `f488ca5`, four days before the 2026-07-06-dated page was written that way; independent pre-existing drift this ingest happened to catch, not part of the #207/#209 diffs themselves), updated `index.md`'s skill table (new `docs-sync` row, corrected the same stale `sync-docs` claim). All new cross-reference links verified resolvable before commit.

## [2026-07-17] ingest | PR #218 (merged `81c8857`) + same-day follow-up fix (`335a382`) ingested as one source page, [[pr_218_discriminating-check-gate]]. Adds `post_evals::validate_discriminating` + `post_evals::_run_formula` to `scripts/post_evals.sh`: a freeze-time gate wired into `/coderails:post-evals` as Step 3b that pipes an eval's optional `fixtures.good`/`fixtures.bad` into the check's formula and rejects any check where the two fixtures don't produce opposite exit codes (good exits 0, bad exits non-zero). Closes a defect class the pre-existing `negative_control` structural check cannot: both checks operate on TEXT (does `negative_control` differ from `cmd` as a string), neither proves the formula's verdict actually tracks real pass/fail input. Motivating real bug, verified against the diff's own test comment: loop 8b69e779's awk formula split `"39/39 suites passed"` under `-F'[ /]'`, landing `$(NF-2)` on the literal word `"suites"` instead of the numerator — exited 1 unconditionally on both a genuine pass and a genuine fail. `hooks/scripts/tests/discriminate.test.sh` (443 lines, 17 cases + CLI dispatch) directly regression-locks this exact formula in case 1. `fixtures` is an optional, scripted-mode-only schema addition — grandfathered: an eval with no `fixtures` field is validated exactly as before this gate existed, zero behaviour change; opt-in per eval, never retroactive. Env-guard distinguishes environmental crashes (127 command-not-found, 142 timeout sentinel, 126 permission-denied, and any exit >=128 signal death) from genuine discrimination verdicts — the follow-up fix broadened this from 127/142-only to the full set (verified: diff hunk `scripts/post_evals.sh` lines 575-588), ordered so the 142-timeout message stays distinct even though 142 also satisfies >=128 (source comment states this ordering is load-bearing; test case 15 is the regression guard). The follow-up fix (same day, folded into this source page rather than a separate one) also closed two gaps the original PR left open: `good`+`bad` were not required together, so an author supplying `good`+`formula` but omitting `bad` got `bad=""` by jq default and could unsafely "prove" discrimination against an empty string nobody wrote (test cases 11/12 construct this exact unsafe-accept shape as proof); and malformed (non-object) `fixtures` degraded silently into a false "non-discriminating" report instead of a distinct error (test case 16). Design context captured verbatim from the task brief and cross-checked against the diff: an earlier hard-stop in the building loop wrongly concluded the feature was unbuildable on a broken classifier's claim that ~91% of the corpus's `negative_control` values looked like prose (near-zero real surface for a fixtures gate); re-measured, the real figure is ~46%; overturned by a `/coderails:disconfirm` pass plus an adversarial fable-5 red-team that challenged the classifier itself. The real design fork — real-surface execution vs. formula-against-fixtures — was decided against real-surface execution because at freeze time a not-yet-built surface and a genuinely broken check both exit non-zero indistinguishably; synthetic fixtures sidestep that ambiguity by exercising the formula against known inputs with known expected outcomes. **Honest boundary, stated prominently on the source page and cross-referenced everywhere this gate is now documented:** validates only fixtures-carrying checks (no retroactive validation of the ~46% of the corpus with scripted checks lacking fixtures, nothing at all for prose/judgement-mode evals); even a pass proves only that the formula CAN discriminate between two specific synthetic inputs, not that it tests the right claim, that `cmd`/`fixtures.formula` stay in sync after later edits, or that the fixtures are representative. Updated [[task-evals-gate]] (new "Discriminating-check gate" section between the anti-gaming-rules section and the loop-scope gate section — mechanism, env-guard, grandfathering, honest boundary, both design-history notes, and an explicit relationship-to-rule-2 paragraph distinguishing text-level from behaviour-level checking), [[task-evals]] (schema section cross-references `fixtures`; rule 2 gained a pointer to the new gate; a new "Discriminating-check gate" subsection added after the anti-gaming rules list), [[post-evals]] (Step 3b inserted into the command sequence, renumbered 7→8 steps; scripts-used list corrected from "second subcommand" to naming `validate-discriminating` as the third, `grade-loop` now the fourth). All three touched pages' frontmatter `sources:`/`tags:`/`last_updated` updated. index.md: new Sources-table bullet appended after the #216/#217 entry (correct chronological order — #218 merged after both), no hooks-table row needed (this PR touches `scripts/post_evals.sh`, a command-chain script, not a `hooks.json`-wired hook).

## [2026-07-17] ingest | PR #232 (`feat/tier-review`, merged `88915bb`) — the tier-review gate. Created [[pr_232_tier-review-gate]] (whole-PR cluster ingest, not per-fix, per this PR's own briefing constraint). Builds `scripts/tier-gate/`: a root-owned macOS LaunchDaemon judging whether an agent's self-classified `tier=0` eval-exemption claim is honest — closing a gap [[task-evals-gate]]'s tier-0 predicate always had (pure self-attestation, nothing reviewed it). The judge sees `{claimed_tier, diff}` only; the defendant's own `tier_justification` prose is never read — this channel was DELETED (`cc5c570`), not hardened. Auth is the owner's Claude subscription (`claude -p` + root-held `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN`, never a metered key) via a root-owned `claude` binary with `HOME`/`cwd` pinned to a root-owned dir. Mechanical model-free prefilter (path denylist + size cap) blocks obvious cases pre-judge. ## [2026-07-20] query-file-back | Query on judge architecture. Synthesis: two judge roles in coderails exist at architectural boundaries where self-grading would create a gap. (1) **workflow-audit judge** — a fresh sonnet subagent assessing n-gram clusters mined from transcripts, fixed-vocabulary input (cluster JSON only), three rejection criteria (project-specific / already-covered / tooling-mechanics), verdict is sole in-session filter. (2) **tier-review judge** — a root-owned macOS LaunchDaemon outside the agent's trust domain (separate uid, root-held auth via owner's subscription, root-owned `curl` for all I/O), judges `tier=0` self-exemption honesty, takes only `{claimed_tier, diff}`, posts a commit status or nothing. Both embody [[enforcement-model]]'s design law (checks by the party with motive to pass them are not checks) and the principle of fixed vocabulary / reject-on-ambiguity. Created [[judge-architecture_2026-07-20]] investigation (6 sections: two judges, design law connection, cross-architecture principle, related links). Updated [[index.md]] Investigations section. ## [2026-07-21] query-file-back | Why skills/dashboard/ is on TIER_GATE_PATH_DENYLIST

Query asked why the dashboard is on the tier-gate path denylist, what the
self-edit denylist protects against, and why the list isn't just
`scripts/tier-gate/`.

Key finding: the query's premise is a slight misread of the code. The regex
is primarily the **outward-facing/irreversible-surface list** — a model-free
restatement of the tier-0 exemption predicate — not a self-edit list. The
self-edit leash in `tg_gate_pr` is a second consumer that explicitly "reuses"
the same regex and names only `scripts/tier-gate/` as the daemon's own source.
Git chronology confirms the borrow direction (denylist in `cc5c570` with the
dashboard already present; leash later in `e8bdd6c`). The dashboard earns its
place independently: a 160-file Next.js app with served endpoints, including
the unauthenticated `POST /api/run` exec surface.

Filed as [[tier-gate-path-denylist-dashboard_2026-07-21]].

the public-release work. The durable content is the tier correction, not the doc:
filed tier 0 on size alone, judge returned `verdict=illegitimate`. Tier 0 also
requires an EXISTING verify-criterion (`judge-prompt.md` predicate 3), which a
brand-new file structurally cannot satisfy at any size. Passing the visible size
cap says nothing about the coverage predicate.

**#256** fixes routine runs leaving no transcript on disk — `runClaude()` returned
output in memory only and never wrote the `outputPath` already in the ledger.
Review found the shipped tests didn't prove the fix: deleting the persist call
turned 3 of 4 red, but *moving* it past the SIGKILL early-return left all 125
green, since the timeout and ENOENT tests never supplied an `outputPath`. Three
tests added, one assertion tightened to the exact ledger path, no production-code
change (125 → 128), each mutation-proved.

Also the **first live firing of the tier-gate DENY path** — `verdict=self_edit`
on `skills/dashboard/`, refusing to judge before reaching the `GO` eval artifact.
Surfaced a legibility defect: `self_edit` posts as `FAILURE` with an empty
description, indistinguishable from a broken build.

Pages: created `sources/pr_254_install-run-log.md`,
`sources/pr_256_runner-transcript-persistence.md`; updated
`design/dashboard-runner.md` (new "Run transcript persistence" section), `index.md`.

## [2026-07-22] lint | Orphan check run correctly for the first time; found and fixed a stale-state contradiction on PR #250 and 2 dead links.

**METHOD CORRECTION (the main finding of this pass).** The 2026-07-20 and 2026-07-21 lints both reported "orphans" that were actually **dead links** — outbound `[[x]]` with no page `x`. The skill defines an orphan as the inverse: a page with zero *inbound* links. That check had never been run in this vault. Both checks were run separately this pass, with `index.md`/`log.md` excluded as link *sources* — including them makes the orphan count trivially zero (index catalogs everything) and the check theatre.

**FINDINGS:**
- **Contradictions: 1 found, 1 fixed.** `sources/pr_250_loop_retro_promotion.md` claimed `**Status:** OPEN (awaiting human merge approval)`. Verified against the live PR: MERGED 2026-07-20T14:39:27Z (`e865cc1`). The page was written pre-merge and the merge was never reflected back — the first case in this vault of a source page outliving the state it recorded. Corrected in three places (Summary, PR state, Related). The design constraint the page documents (ruleset `bypass actors: none` blocks routine self-merge) is unchanged and still real; only the terminal state was wrong.
- **The pre-existing `⚠️ CONTRADICTION` on [[discipline-loop]] re-verified, still accurate.** Read `hooks/scripts/lib/discipline_common.sh` on current main: `dc_extract_last_text` still runs the two-stage `jq -R 'fromjson? // empty' | jq -s` with **no** `select(type == "object")` guard. Flag is live, not stale — do not clear it. Owned by the parked jq-slurp round-2 arc.
- **True orphans: 6, all benign.** `skills/handoff.md`, `sources/pr_19-30_...`, `pr_215_...`, `pr_250_...`, `pr_254_...`, `pr_49_...`. Every one is catalogued in `index.md`; they lack only content-page-to-content-page inbound links. For `sources/` pages that is the expected shape — a PR record is reached via the index, not cited by peers, unless a later PR builds on it. No action.
- **Dead links: 2 fixed, rest classified.** `sources/pr_204_cost-reporter.md` used `[[design/enforcement-model|enforcement-model]]` — a path-prefixed target that does not resolve by basename; corrected to `[[enforcement-model]]`. `sources/pr_250_...` linked `[[judge-architecture]]`, but investigation pages are date-stamped per schema; corrected to `[[judge-architecture_2026-07-20]]`, which also cleared that page's orphan status. Remaining dead targets are in `log.md` only (append-only, correctly left) or are genuine non-page prose: bash fragments (`[[-n "$untracked"]]`), schema meta-text (`[[wiki-links]]`, `[[link]]`, `[[page_name]]`), and deliberate cross-vault pointers into assistant-agent-wiki (`[[capabilities/send-gate]]`, `[[capabilities/inbox-brief]]`) — carried forward from the 2026-07-21 classification, unchanged.
- **Index gap: 1 fixed.** `pr_250_loop_retro_promotion` had **zero** inbound links including from `index.md` — the only vault page entirely absent from the catalog. Added to the Sources section in merge-date order (between #240 and #254).
- **Stale pages: 0.** Six pages predate the 30-day cutoff (2026-06-22), all date-stamped point-in-time records — 2 `investigations/` and 4 `sources/session_*`, immutable by schema. Not staleness.
- **Frontmatter: 100% compliant.** All 205 pages carry `last_updated`.
- **Missing cross-references: swept, none actionable.** A bare-mention scan flagged 105 pages, spot-checked and rejected as heuristic noise: the hits are slash-command references in prose and tables (`/wiki-ingest`, `coderails:systematic-debugging`), which are correctly not wiki-linked.

**SUGGESTIONS (ingest-class, not lint fixes — deliberately not authored here):**
- `learned-failure-modes.md` and `docs/coderails/specs/tier-review-spec.md` both live in the plugin repo and are referenced across several pages with no wiki page. The tier-review spec is the higher-value ingest: it is cited as the authority for the ruleset's `bypass actors: none` design, and that claim currently has no in-vault target.
- `skills/fable-mode.md` — shipped 2026-07-08, still no skill page.
- The 2026-07-15 `workflow-audit` SKILL rewrite (commit `a6d0142`, removed the approval gate) has no `sources/` page; carried from the 2026-07-16 lint.
- **Process suggestion with teeth:** PR #250's stale `OPEN` status is a repeatable ingest failure mode, not a one-off — any page written while a PR is in flight can outlive its own state. Worth a lint check that re-reads `gh pr view` for every `sources/pr_*` page whose body asserts a non-merged status.

**VERIFICATION:** 205 pages. Post-fix re-run of the link graph: 0 dead links from any content page, 6 orphans (all index-covered, all benign). Committed directly to vault (`git.worktree: false`).

### [2026-07-22] lint addendum | stale-status sweep across all 120 wiki-documented PRs — 0 further contradictions, 1 durable gotcha recorded

Having found PR #250's stale `OPEN` above, the sweep for siblings was run rather than deferred (it is the "claims superseded by newer sources" check, not future work). Every PR number appearing in a `sources/pr_*.md` filename (120 distinct) was reconciled against live GitHub state.

**Result: 0 further stale-status contradictions.** PR #250 was the only genuine instance.

**Two probe defects worth recording, both mine, both caught before they became findings:**
1. **cwd drift.** The first sweep ran `gh pr list` from inside the wiki vault, so it resolved against `blueman82/coderails-wiki` (12 PRs) instead of `blueman82/coderails` (257) — producing 115 false `NOT_FOUND` hits including PR #250, which had been directly verified as MERGED minutes earlier. That contradiction with a known-good fact is what exposed the broken probe. The trap is that a wrong-repo `gh` query returns a *plausible* answer, not an error. Anchor `gh` with `--repo` from a vault shell.
2. **Truncated page.** `--limit 400` on a 257-PR repo was fine, but the vault query's 12-row result made the truncation invisible. Check the row count against the expected population before trusting a set-difference.

**The durable gotcha — PR numbers before 2026-07-05 do not resolve on GitHub.** After the two true hits (#74, #79) came back `CLOSED` with titles totally unrelated to their wiki pages (`dashboard: make side rails scrollable`, `fix(dashboard): sync package-lock` vs. the pages' watchdog-stall and sync-docs-drift subjects), the cause is the 2026-07-05 repo recreation recorded in the repo's own local notes: the old repo was **deleted and recreated** to strip `refs/pull/*` carrying a retired author identity, so PR numbering restarted and the current #74/#79 are different, later PRs that happen to reuse the numbers. The wiki pages are **correct** — `git log` shows `6fe5f94 Merge pull request #74 from blueman82/bug/config-test-watchdog-slow` and `68ce312 Merge pull request #79 from blueman82/docs/sync-docs-drift-fixes`, both on main, both matching their pages' subjects. No page edited.

Corollary for future lints and any `gh`-based audit: **`gh pr view <N>` is only authoritative for PRs merged after 2026-07-05.** Below that boundary, verify by merge commit (`git log --grep="Merge pull request #<N>"`) and branch name, never by PR number — and the commit SHAs cited in pre-2026-07-05 source pages are equally dead, since the same operation rewrote every SHA (a `git filter-repo` mailmap pass). A page citing a SHA that `git log` cannot resolve is not evidence of a wrong page.

This retires lint suggestion #4 above (the proposed `gh pr view` re-read check): it is worth running, but only above the 2026-07-05 boundary, or it manufactures ~110 false positives.

### [2026-07-22] docs-sync | IN FLIGHT — PR #258 (hook-table drift), plus a higher-severity deferred finding in `docs/TIER-GATE.md`

Nightly docs-sync. Audit found four drift items, all in git-tracked in-scope `.md`, all verified against `hooks/hooks.json` and the hook scripts as ground truth:

1. `README.md` "## Hooks" table had no row for `crack_on_prose_gate.sh` — added.
2. `docs/REFERENCE.md` "## Hook Activation Matrix" had no row for the same hook — added.
3. `INSTALLATION.md` "The one UserPromptSubmit hook" — two are registered (`inject_context.sh`, `crack_on_gate.sh`); corrected.
4. `INSTALLATION.md` "Four Stop hooks block via exit 2" — five do (adding `crack_on_prose_gate`); and "On PreToolUse, five hooks can block" — six do (adding `crack_on_gate` on `AskUserQuestion`, which blocks via `permissionDecision: deny`, matching REFERENCE.md's own matrix definition of block). Both corrected.

The hook has been registered in `hooks.json` since PR #238 (2026-07-17) and documented in `AGENTS.md` all along — the omission was confined to README and REFERENCE. This is the same drift class the 2026-07-18 lint predicted as "a candidate for a docs-sync follow-up."

**REPORT-ONLY, HIGHER SEVERITY THAN ANYTHING FIXED THIS RUN — `docs/TIER-GATE.md` is wrong about tier semantics, in a way that will actively mislead a contributor.** Found while verifying why this PR's own merge needs a tier-review status. Two distinct defects:

- **Tier definitions are inverted.** `docs/TIER-GATE.md` says tier 0 is "user-facing changes, architecture, API changes, security, breaking changes" and tier 2 is "risk-free changes (comments, formatting, trivial config)". The authoritative judge prompt (`scripts/tier-gate/judge-prompt.md`, lines 22-46) says the opposite: tier 0 is the *exempt* tier requiring single work-unit + no outward surface + existing coverage, and "a user-facing change is NEVER tier 0, even if trivial"; tier 2 is the *full suite* (3+ work-units or an irreversible surface). A contributor following TIER-GATE.md would claim exactly the wrong tier and be rejected by the daemon.
- **Gate scope is stale.** `docs/TIER-GATE.md` describes the layer-1 local merge gate as applying to tier-0 claims only. The merge script's own comment (lines 123-127) states the daemon "now judges EVERY tier, not just tier 0, so this gate runs at every tier too (no more PR_EVAL_TIER == 0 restriction)", and the tier-gate runner parses tier=([0-2]). Confirmed live: this run's own tier-1 PR requires a tier-review status before it can merge.

Not fixed this run, deliberately: PR #258's evals were frozen and graded against a three-file scope before this was found, and eval E3 asserts the diff is exactly those three files. Folding in a fourth file would staleify the SHA-bound review and eval artifacts and break a P0. The routine is single-delivery by structure, and a second delivery risks a trailing `abort=` marker turning a clean merge red under the run log's last-marker predicate. The next nightly run re-discovers it and ships it as its own clean delivery. Logged to the run log as `finding=deferred`.

**Also report-only, carried forward unchanged:** `INSTALLATION.md`'s "What you get" table still enumerates 25 of 36 shipped skills. Left unfixed for the same reason the 2026-07-17 run gave — reworking a curated summary table into an exhaustive list is a content-design judgment, not mechanical drift, and line 111's "see the full list" parenthetical already frames the table as non-exhaustive.

**Two candidate items examined and declined as NOT drift:** (a) INSTALLATION.md's "the same two content-discipline checks also run on SubagentStop" — three hooks are registered on `SubagentStop`, but `offload_push_guard.sh` only emits additionalContext and exits 0, so it is a nudge, not a content-discipline check; the sentence is true as scoped. (b) `docs/INSTALL-RUN-LOG.md` — a dated record of one install run on 2026-07-20, not a description of current behaviour, so it cannot go stale the way a behaviour description does.

**Gate chain:** branch `docs/hook-table-drift` off freshly-fetched `529c77c`; task-evals frozen PRE-edit at tier 1 (E1–E3 scripted + E4 agent-run, all P0). The freeze-time smoke-run executed every eval command and negative control for real, which caught and removed a broken E0 whose wrapper inverted its own exit code — found pre-freeze, so rewritten rather than amended. Discriminating-check fixtures on E1/E3 both split good/bad correctly. Manifest three-dot `--name-status` clean (3 paths, all in-scope `.md`, none deny-listed, no rename/copy/delete), independently confirmed against GitHub's own file list for the PR. E4 graded by a fresh subagent given only the eval and artifact refs.

**Review outcome (pr-review-toolkit comment-analyzer): approve, one optional suggestion, taken.** The reviewer independently re-derived the 2/5/6 counts, confirmed both tables now cover all 16 registered hook scripts, and ran the hook's own fixture suite at `hooks/scripts/tests/crack_on_prose_gate.test.sh` — which passes and empirically confirms the cap behaviour (blocks on attempts 1-3, allows attempt 4 logged capped=1, counter resets per turn), the unwritable-counter fail-open, and the SubagentStop out-of-scope path. Its one suggestion: INSTALLATION.md's one-line summary stated the hook's function with no ceiling while README and REFERENCE both carried one. Taken — a caveat naming the no-interrogative-marker miss and the per-turn cap of 3 was added. That moved the head from `ed57576` to `edc3baf`, so the frozen scripted evals were re-run at the new head (E1/E2/E3 all green, manifest unchanged) and E4 was reset to pending and sent to a FRESH grader per the amendment rule, rather than carrying the earlier verdict forward.

**One probe defect of my own, recorded:** my initial in-scope enumeration missed `docs/INSTALL-RUN-LOG.md` entirely; I only read it because a subagent's report happened to name it. The glob-driven file list I built was never reconciled against `git ls-files` output. Same class as the cwd-drift entry above — a plausible-looking enumeration is not a verified one.

## [2026-07-22] ingest | PR #259 (`3de997b`) merged: remember-plugin memory-injection cap guard, and the recovery of the lost 7th token-burn measure. Created [[pr_259_remember-inject-cap-guard]] (source), [[remember_inject_cap_guard]] (hook), [[plugin-boundary-writes]] (design). The 2026-07-17 token-burn effort shipped **seven** measures; six landed as PRs (#228 = rows 1–4, #229 = row 6, #230 = row 7) and row 5 was applied BY HAND to a file inside the remember plugin's version-pinned cache directory, committed nowhere. It was nearly lost on 2026-07-22 — recoverable only by searching every Claude Code transcript on disk, since it appeared in no PR, issue, commit message or repo file, and the surviving prose in `skills/agentic-loop/SKILL.md` had been renumbered to "row N of 4", erasing that seven ever existed. Filed a `⚠️ CONTRADICTION` notice on [[pr_228_229_230_token-burn-reduction-and-agents-split]] correcting the denominator (rows 1–4 **of 7**) without disputing what #228 shipped. PR #259 makes the patch survivable: canonical text now in git under `hooks/patches/` (with honest provenance — `vendor.txt` is a *reconstructed* pristine copy, recovered by reverse-applying the hand patch, validated by a round-trip inverse test), plus a `SessionStart` hook that detects the cap's absence. Design decision recorded on [[plugin-boundary-writes]]: built to auto-write by default, four review agents audited it and one demonstrated live that auto-write is indefensible for a public plugin (coderails would silently rewrite an official-marketplace plugin's file on any user's machine, applying one maintainer's personal tuning constant as though it were a bug fix; and on any version with a differing file shape the guard warns but never stamps, so an identical warning fires every session forever with no opt-out). Resolved to warn-only by default, writing gated behind `REMEMBER_INJECT_CAP_AUTOWRITE=1`, warn suppressed once per plugin version via a stamp under `$HOME/.claude/coderails/` — deliberately NOT under `~/.claude/plugins/`, since writing bookkeeping into the other party's tree is the same boundary violation the default exists to prevent. Two review findings carried as engineering lessons rather than PR trivia: (1) detection was a bare substring grep for `REMEMBER_INJECT_MAX_BYTES`, satisfied by any mention at all, so the hook exited silently concluding the cap was present while the truncation code was absent — the exact condition the hook exists to detect, swallowed by the check meant to detect it; the PR's own test used a stronger definition (the truncation line) than production did, which is a standing tell; fixed to key on evidence of the patch. (2) A regression test wrapped in a live-plugin-cache check printed `skip` while the suite still reported PASS — and because the repo's test gate auto-discovers `*.test.sh` by glob, the gate reported green against the exact bug the test was written to prevent, on any fresh clone; proven by mutation (reintroduce the bug → 3 failures normally, `skip`+PASS with `HOME` pointed at an empty dir) and made hermetic. The historical bug those tests guard is itself instructive: a shape check counted occurrences of the patch block's last line — a bare `fi`, appearing 8 times in the real `session-start-hook.sh` — so the guard refused to patch the very file it existed for, and small fixtures with one `fi` hid it. Updated [[install-and-cache-trap]] (new foreign-plugin section: the same version-pinned-cache trap when the perishable file belongs to another maintainer) and [[index]] (hooks table row, design entry, sources entry, plus a note that [[discipline-loop]]'s "1 SessionStart / 20 commands" count is now one short and its body has not been recounted). Accuracy caveat recorded on all three new pages: the opt-in is **not** enabled on this machine — `REMEMBER_INJECT_CAP_AUTOWRITE` could not be written to `~/.claude/settings.json` because a harness gate blocks agent edits to that file, so writing is currently OFF locally and the cap will not auto-reapply after a remember bump until it is added by hand.

## [2026-07-22] ingest | PRs #260 (`900c740`), #263 (`7ff7967`) — dashboard security review

Six Low-severity findings in `skills/dashboard/`, all fixed in #260: queue-path
`inputAllowed` check missing in the sweep path (F1), a hash path-traversal via an
object spread carrying the wrong field (F2), a config loader missing array/type
guards on a value used as a lock filename (F3), loose directory/file permissions
from `mkdirSync`'s mode being a no-op on an existing dir (F4), a documentation-only
config-trust-tier note (F5), and a non-timing-safe token compare (F6). #263 removed
the review doc from the tracked tree (still readable from history). Threat-model
reframing: nothing here crosses a privilege boundary (`~/.claude` dirs are
`drwx------`), so findings were graded down rather than inflated. Eight defences
attacked and held (argv injection, DNS rebinding, path traversal, exec-lock TOCTOU,
osascript escalation, hash re-validation, SSE framing, read-only tool allowlist).
Most consequential finding: MERGED ≠ DEPLOYED — the launchd routine-sweeper ran the
sweeper from a working checkout 57 commits behind `origin/main`, so F1's fix was
absent from the code actually running; proven live-fire (unauthorized queue intent
reached a real `--dangerously-skip-permissions` invocation, no damage only by the
invoked skill's own judgement, not by any gate).
